Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

No user interaction (extension)



<span class="line"><!---->No user interaction (extension)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





0. Apply a patch for one of the two vulnerabilities.(The process race patch is recommended as this is the default json parsing function)



<span class="line"><!---->0. Apply a patch for one of the two vulnerabilities.(The process race patch is recommended as this is the default json parsing function)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





1. Host index.html with a web server: python3 -m http.server 8000



<span class="line"><!---->1. Host index.html with a web server: python3 -m http.server 8000<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





2. Install the attached extension (ext) and allow in incognito



<span class="line"><!---->2. Install the attached extension (ext) and allow in incognito<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





3. run ./out/release/chrome -enable-blink-features=MojoJS --user-data-dir=./userdata --load-extension=/path/to/ext



<span class="line"><!---->3. run ./out/release/chrome -enable-blink-features=MojoJS --user-data-dir=./userdata --load-extension=/path/to/ext<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





see the attachment for the reproduced video, note that I omitted the step of and allow ext in incognito



<span class="line"><!---->see the attachment for the reproduced video, note that I omitted the step of and allow ext in incognito<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





**Note: Allow incognito is just needed because I'm using the chrome.windows api to simulate closing a browser window.**



<span class="line"><!---->**Note: Allow incognito is just needed because I'm using the chrome.windows api to simulate closing a browser window.**<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





User interaction (exit browser)



<span class="line"><!---->User interaction (exit browser)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





0. Apply a patch for one of the two vulnerabilities.(The process race patch is recommended as this is the default json parsing function)



<span class="line"><!---->0. Apply a patch for one of the two vulnerabilities.(The process race patch is recommended as this is the default json parsing function)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





1. Host index.html with a web server: python3 -m http.server 8000



<span class="line"><!---->1. Host index.html with a web server: python3 -m http.server 8000<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





2. Open incognito browser (**can be another chrome instance, guest view, etc - we just need two Profile instances**)



<span class="line"><!---->2. Open incognito browser (**can be another chrome instance, guest view, etc - we just need two Profile instances**)<!----></span>

<br>



<br>

<span class="line"><!---->4. close incognito browser<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Problem Description:



<b class="line"><!---->Problem Description:<!----></b>



<br>





## Root Cause with two UAF pattern



<span class="line"><!---->## Root Cause with two UAF pattern<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This vulnerability is similar to two issue:



<span class="line"><!---->This vulnerability is similar to two issue:<!----></span>



<br>





https://bugs.chromium.org/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1289523



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://bugs.chromium.org/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1289523"><!---->https://bugs.chromium.org/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1289523<!----></a>



<br>





https://bugs.chromium.org/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1233942



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://bugs.chromium.org/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1233942"><!---->https://bugs.chromium.org/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1233942<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





[0] InterestGroupPermissionsChecker is a field of InterestGroupManagerImpl and is owned by StoragePartitionImpl, so it is bound to the life cycle of the Profile, and when the Profile is released, InterestGroupPermissionsChecker is also released.



<span class="line"><!---->[0] InterestGroupPermissionsChecker is a field of InterestGroupManagerImpl and is owned by StoragePartitionImpl, so it is bound to the life cycle of the Profile, and when the Profile is released, InterestGroupPermissionsChecker is also released.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





[1] InterestGroupPermissionsChecker::OnRequestComplete binds base::Unretained(this) to InterestGroupPermissionsChecker::OnJsonParsed callback，and as a callback parameter to ParseJson.



<span class="line"><!---->[1] InterestGroupPermissionsChecker::OnRequestComplete binds base::Unretained(this) to InterestGroupPermissionsChecker::OnJsonParsed callback，and as a callback parameter to ParseJson.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





**There are two paths in DataDecoder::ParseJson that can cause UAF.**



<span class="line"><!---->**There are two paths in DataDecoder::ParseJson that can cause UAF.**<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





### First place: **thread callback race pattern**



<span class="line"><!---->### First place: **thread callback race pattern**<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





If we enable BUILD_RUST_JSON_PARSER when compiling



<span class="line"><!---->If we enable BUILD_RUST_JSON_PARSER when compiling<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





[2] The `callback with Unretained InterestGroupPermissionsChecker raw ptr` is posted to a separate sequence in threadpool.



<span class="line"><!---->[2] The `callback with Unretained InterestGroupPermissionsChecker raw ptr` is posted to a separate sequence in threadpool.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





[3] InterestGroupPermissionsChecker may be destroyed in UI thread when ReadAndReturnValueWithError run in threadpool.



<span class="line"><!---->[3] InterestGroupPermissionsChecker may be destroyed in UI thread when ReadAndReturnValueWithError run in threadpool.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





And when ParsingComplete is sent back to UI thread, it will be executed to InterestGroupPermissionsChecker::OnJsonParsed callback(bind Unretained InterestGroupPermissionsChecker raw ptr), thus triggering UAF.



<span class="line"><!---->And when ParsingComplete is sent back to UI thread, it will be executed to InterestGroupPermissionsChecker::OnJsonParsed callback(bind Unretained InterestGroupPermissionsChecker raw ptr), thus triggering UAF.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





### Second place: **process callback race pattern**



<span class="line"><!---->### Second place: **process callback race pattern**<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





by default



<span class="line"><!---->by default<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





[4] ParseJson will use callback with Unretained InterestGroupPermissionsChecker raw ptr to create a reference counted request, so even if the profile is released, the request will not be released, the mojo connection will not be disconnected, and the request will have callback as one of its fields callback_ save.



<span class="line"><!---->[4] ParseJson will use callback with Unretained InterestGroupPermissionsChecker raw ptr to create a reference counted request, so even if the profile is released, the request will not be released, the mojo connection will not be disconnected, and the request will have callback as one of its fields callback_ save.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





[5] The JsonParserImpl::Parse function in the service process will be called through mojo.



<span class="line"><!---->[5] The JsonParserImpl::Parse function in the service process will be called through mojo.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





[6] While Parse is executing asynchronously in the service process, we close the window in the browser process to release the Profile and the associated InterestGroupPermissionsChecker.



<span class="line"><!---->[6] While Parse is executing asynchronously in the service process, we close the window in the browser process to release the Profile and the associated InterestGroupPermissionsChecker.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





When the service process finishes executing JsonParserImpl::Parse, it will send the result back to the browser process through callback.



<span class="line"><!---->When the service process finishes executing JsonParserImpl::Parse, it will send the result back to the browser process through callback.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





[7] This will eventually call the callback with Unretained InterestGroupPermissionsChecker raw ptr in the OnServiceValueOrError function, triggering the UAF.



<span class="line"><!---->[7] This will eventually call the callback with Unretained InterestGroupPermissionsChecker raw ptr in the OnServiceValueOrError function, triggering the UAF.<!----></span>



<br>

	...



<span class="line"><!---->	...<!----></span>



<br>





  DataDecoder::ResultCallback<V> callback_; 



<span class="line"><!---->  DataDecoder::ResultCallback&lt;V&gt; callback_; <!----></span>



<br>





};



<span class="line"><!---->};<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





## Other



<span class="line"><!---->## Other<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Explain the patch.



<span class="line"><!---->Explain the patch.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This vulnerability can obviously be triggered by mojojs using a compromise render, but since I haven't been able to construct the parameters of the mojo interface well, I can only patch some checks to execute the vulnerable code, but the vulnerable code is obviously OK Triggered by normal function.



<span class="line"><!---->This vulnerability can obviously be triggered by mojojs using a compromise render, but since I haven't been able to construct the parameters of the mojo interface well, I can only patch some checks to execute the vulnerable code, but the vulnerable code is obviously OK Triggered by normal function.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In addition, I added sleep to JsonParserImpl::Parse or JSONReader::ReadAndReturnValueWithError to block it, which makes it easier to trigger this vulnerability.



<span class="line"><!---->In addition, I added sleep to JsonParserImpl::Parse or JSONReader::ReadAndReturnValueWithError to block it, which makes it easier to trigger this vulnerability.<!----></span>



<br>





But this can obviously be blocked by constructing an extremely large json parameter, increasing the possibility of successful competition.



<span class="line"><!---->But this can obviously be blocked by constructing an extremely large json parameter, increasing the possibility of successful competition.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Because this vulnerability can be triggered by a plug-in without interaction, and the message loop can be blocked by sending a large json parameter or sending a large number of ipc messages, so as to control the timing of use.



<span class="line"><!---->Because this vulnerability can be triggered by a plug-in without interaction, and the message loop can be blocked by sending a large json parameter or sending a large number of ipc messages, so as to control the timing of use.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





So I think inducing users to install a malicious plugin that does not require any permissions will most likely lead to remote code execution, which is a serious vulnerability.



<span class="line"><!---->So I think inducing users to install a malicious plugin that does not require any permissions will most likely lead to remote code execution, which is a serious vulnerability.<!----></span>



<br>

Thanks for the report.



<span class="line"><!---->Thanks for the report.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





A UAF that requires a browser patch in order to trigger is always something we have to question, because the PoC doesn't really demonstrate that it's a reachable bug in Chrome. If it was just sleeps to rig race conditions that would be one thing, but there are functional changes to that code.



<span class="line"><!---->A UAF that requires a browser patch in order to trigger is always something we have to question, because the PoC doesn't really demonstrate that it's a reachable bug in Chrome. If it was just sleeps to rig race conditions that would be one thing, but there are functional changes to that code.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





That said, passing a base::Unretained in the DataDecoder::ParseJson callback does look like a bug and should be fixed.



<span class="line"><!---->That said, passing a base::Unretained in the DataDecoder::ParseJson callback does look like a bug and should be fixed.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Setting at Security_Severity-High based on the need for an extension or compromised renderer, but if the race condition is really hard to hit then this could be lower.



<span class="line"><!---->Setting at Security_Severity-High based on the need for an extension or compromised renderer, but if the race condition is really hard to hit then this could be lower.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





mmenke@: The fix is trivial, as the reporter notes, but do you have any concerns? Or else thoughts on reachability of this bug, given the patches needed to repro?



<span class="line"><!---->mmenke@: The fix is trivial, as the reporter notes, but do you have any concerns? Or else thoughts on reachability of this bug, given the patches needed to repro?<!----></span>

[+rsesek]:  DataDecoder has no docs on safe usage.  I had thought that "Encapsulates an exclusive connection to an isolated instance of the Data Decoder service" meant that deleting a DataDecoder would be analogous to tearing down a Mojo pipe, so no weak pointers would be needed.  It looks like it creates its own remotes...but wraps them in a refcounted objects in order to invoke callbacks after the DataDecoder itself is destroyed?  This seems unexpected to me.



<span class="line"><!---->[+rsesek]:  DataDecoder has no docs on safe usage.  I had thought that "Encapsulates an exclusive connection to an isolated instance of the Data Decoder service" meant that deleting a DataDecoder would be analogous to tearing down a Mojo pipe, so no weak pointers would be needed.  It looks like it creates its own remotes...but wraps them in a refcounted objects in order to invoke callbacks after the DataDecoder itself is destroyed?  This seems unexpected to me.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I had assumed the difference between the static and non-static methods was precisely around the non-static API calls not invoking callbacks after the destruction of the DataDecoder.



<span class="line"><!---->I had assumed the difference between the static and non-static methods was precisely around the non-static API calls not invoking callbacks after the destruction of the DataDecoder.<!----></span>

[rsesek]:  Actually, the description of the bug seems to directly contradict the API description:



<span class="line"><!---->[rsesek]:  Actually, the description of the bug seems to directly contradict the API description:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





  // Note that |callback| will only be called if the parsing operation succeeds



<span class="line"><!---->  // Note that |callback| will only be called if the parsing operation succeeds<!----></span>



<br>





  // or fails before this DataDecoder is destroyed.



<span class="line"><!---->  // or fails before this DataDecoder is destroyed.<!----></span>



<br>





  void ParseJson(const std::string& json, ValueParseCallback callback);



<span class="line"><!---->  void ParseJson(const std::string&amp; json, ValueParseCallback callback);<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





That implies this method should be safe to call as InterestGroupPermissionsChecker does, with base::Unretained(this), where `this` owns the DataDecoder.  I think this is a DataDecoder bug.



<span class="line"><!---->That implies this method should be safe to call as InterestGroupPermissionsChecker does, with base::Unretained(this), where `this` owns the DataDecoder.  I think this is a DataDecoder bug.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Am I missing something?



<span class="line"><!---->Am I missing something?<!----></span>

>> creates its own remotes, but wraps them in a refcounted objects in order to invoke callbacks after the DataDecoder itself is destroyed

<span class="line"><!---->Could you try to check it like this, thank you very much :)<!----></span>

content/browser/interest_group/interest_group_permissions_checker.cc



<span class="line"><!---->content/browser/interest_group/interest_group_permissions_checker.cc<!----></span>

Date: Fri May 20 19:04:11 2022



<span class="line"><!---->Date: Fri May 20 19:04:11 2022<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





[FLEDGE] Don't use DataDecoder objects.



<span class="line"><!---->[FLEDGE] Don't use DataDecoder objects.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Instead use DataDecoder::ParseJSONIsolated, which doesn't use an object.



<span class="line"><!---->Instead use DataDecoder::ParseJSONIsolated, which doesn't use an object.<!----></span>



<br>





DataDecoder appears to be broken, in that is can invoke callbacks passed



<span class="line"><!---->DataDecoder appears to be broken, in that is can invoke callbacks passed<!----></span>



<br>





to it after it is destroyed, which violates its API contract.



<span class="line"><!---->to it after it is destroyed, which violates its API contract.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





InterestGroupPermissionsChecker doesn't actually need it. I had been



<span class="line"><!---->InterestGroupPermissionsChecker doesn't actually need it. I had been<!----></span>



<br>





thinking we'd make operations individually cancellable, to better handle



<span class="line"><!---->thinking we'd make operations individually cancellable, to better handle<!----></span>



<br>





having too many headless requests on navigate away, which is why I was



<span class="line"><!---->having too many headless requests on navigate away, which is why I was<!----></span>



<br>





using it in the first place. However, I decided a simpler approach



<span class="line"><!---->using it in the first place. However, I decided a simpler approach<!----></span>



<br>





would work well enough, so ParseJSONIsolated with a weak pointer works



<span class="line"><!---->would work well enough, so ParseJSONIsolated with a weak pointer works<!----></span>



<br>





just as well, and possibly with lower overhead.



<span class="line"><!---->just as well, and possibly with lower overhead.<!----></span>



<br>

Based on 



<span class="line"><!---->Based on <!----></span>





#c13



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="#c13"><!---->#c13<!----></a>





, this particular call site might be unreachable on stable so this might be Security_Impact-None. However, DataDecoder::ParseJSON has 13 call sites so there's a reasonable chance that this is reachable some other way, so we should probably regard it as impactful until proven otherwise. WDYT, kenrb?



<span class="line"><!---->, this particular call site might be unreachable on stable so this might be Security_Impact-None. However, DataDecoder::ParseJSON has 13 call sites so there's a reasonable chance that this is reachable some other way, so we should probably regard it as impactful until proven otherwise. WDYT, kenrb?<!----></span>

If we consider that the data decoder service is the root of the problem here, this hasn't change for a while, so flipping to FoundIn-100 and removing ReleaseBlock-Stable (which was added because this was labelled as a regression).

DataDecoder: Implement callback lifetime guarantees as documented.



<span class="line"><!---->DataDecoder: Implement callback lifetime guarantees as documented.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The DataDecoder instance-based API says that callbacks "will only be



<span class="line"><!---->The DataDecoder instance-based API says that callbacks "will only be<!----></span>



<br>





called if the parsing operation succeeds or fails before this



<span class="line"><!---->called if the parsing operation succeeds or fails before this<!----></span>



<br>





DataDecoder is destroyed." However, this is not what the implementation



<span class="line"><!---->DataDecoder is destroyed." However, this is not what the implementation<!----></span>



<br>





currently does: nothing binds the lifetime of the DataDecoder instance



<span class="line"><!---->currently does: nothing binds the lifetime of the DataDecoder instance<!----></span>



<br>





to the callback. That makes it potentially unsafe to store an instance



<span class="line"><!---->to the callback. That makes it potentially unsafe to store an instance<!----></span>



<br>





of a DataDecoder as a member variable and then bind Unretained



<span class="line"><!---->of a DataDecoder as a member variable and then bind Unretained<!----></span>



<br>





`this` pointers to the DataDecoder callbacks.



<span class="line"><!---->`this` pointers to the DataDecoder callbacks.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This change adds a cancellation flag to DataDecoder requests so that the



<span class="line"><!---->This change adds a cancellation flag to DataDecoder requests so that the<!----></span>



<br>





API guarantees are fulfilled.



<span class="line"><!---->API guarantees are fulfilled.<!----></span>

<br>



<br>





This issue has been flagged as a merge candidate for Chrome OS' LTS channel. If selected, our merge team will handle any additional merges. To help us determine if this issue requires a merge to LTS, please answer this short questionnaire:



<span class="line"><!---->This issue has been flagged as a merge candidate for Chrome OS' LTS channel. If selected, our merge team will handle any additional merges. To help us determine if this issue requires a merge to LTS, please answer this short questionnaire:<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->1. Was this issue a regression for the milestone it was found in?<!----></span>

*** Boilerplate reminders! ***



<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.
